                        cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical Insight into the Sodium-Ion Storage Mechanism on a Hard Carbon Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Xiaoyang; Fang, Youlong; Tian, Jiyu; Lu, Haiyan; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">16</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">18914-18922</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon (HC) has been actively investigated as a high-capacity and low-cost anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs); however, its sodium-storage mechanism has remained controversial, which imposes great difficulties in the design and construction of better microstructured HC materials.  To obtain a deeper understanding of the Na-storage mechanism, we comparatively investigated electrochem. behaviors of HC and graphite for Na- and Li-storage reactions.  The exptl. results reveal that the Na-storage reaction on HC at a low-potential plateau proceeds in a manner similar to the Li+-insertion reaction on graphite but very differently from the Li+-storage process on HC, suggesting that the Na-storage mechanism of HC at a low-voltage plateau operates through the Na+ intercalation into the graphitic layers for the formation of sodium-graphite intercalation compds.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Insight into Sodium Insertion and the Storage Mechanism in Hard Carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Anji Reddy, M.; Helen, M.; Gross, Axel; Fichtner, Maximilian; Euchner, Holger</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">While the technol. importance of carbon-based anodes for sodium-ion batteries is undebated, the underlying mechanism for sodium insertion and storage is still strongly disputed.  Here, a joint exptl. and theor. study is presented that allows to provide detailed insights into the process of Na insertion in nongraphitizable (hard) carbon.  For this purpose, the data from in situ Raman scattering of Na insertion in hard carbon are combined with d. functional theory-based lattice dynamics and band structure calcns. for Na insertion in graphitic model structures used for a local description of graphitic domains in hard carbon.  The agreement of exptl. results and computational findings yields a clear picture of the Na insertion mechanism, which can be described by four different stages that are dominated by surface morphol., defect concn., bulk structure, and nanoporosity.  On the basis of the resulting model for sodium insertion, design strategies are suggested to maximize the capacity of hard carbon.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoA_kOfSPHVi7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhu5tnV3vKtrA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvFChsb7L&amp;md5=69d1c4978e6674e6d15b7fa167c0adc7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms5033"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Matsuda, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ishii, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cumings, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Expanded graphite as superior anode for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Nat.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Expanded graphite as superior anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wen, Yang; He, Kai; Zhu, Yujie; Han, Fudong; Xu, Yunhua; Matsuda, Isamu; Ishii, Yoshitaka; Cumings, John; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite, as the most common anode for com. Li-ion batteries, has been reported to have a very low capacity when used as a Na-ion battery anode.  It is well known that electrochem. insertion of Na+ into graphite is significantly hindered by the insufficient interlayer spacing.  Here we report expanded graphite as a Na-ion battery anode.  Prepd. through a process of oxidn. and partial redn. on graphite, expanded graphite has an enlarged interlayer lattice distance of 4.3 Å yet retains an analogous long-range-ordered layered structure to graphite.  In situ transmission electron microscopy has demonstrated that the Na-ion can be reversibly inserted into and extd. from expanded graphite.  Galvanostatic studies show that expanded graphite can deliver a high reversible capacity of 284 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 20 mA g-1, maintain a capacity of 184 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, and retain 73.92% of its capacity after 2,000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFEZ8wJYk1irVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lixsmPE9TaIlQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXksVeqs7g%253D&amp;md5=e4bc2edac8d22121e7986e165b7df007</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2019.123576"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alvin, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chandra, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Extended plateau capacity of phosphorus-doped hard carbon used as an anode in Na- and K-ion batteries</span>. <i>Chemical Engineering Journal</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>391</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">123576</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Extended plateau capacity of phosphorus-doped hard carbon used as an anode in Na- and K-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Alvin, Stevanus; Chandra, Christian; Kim, Jaehoon</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">391</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">123576</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard C is one of most promising anode materials used in Na-ion batteries (SIBs) because of its high low-voltage plateau capacity.  Heteroatom doping into the C structure is considered an effective method to enhance the Na+-ion uptake.  However, heteroatom doping is not used to increase the low-voltage plateau capacity because the carbonization temps. are limited to low values (600 - 1100°).  The formation of excess defect sites, which is caused by heteroatom doping leads to lower initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE).  Herein, to increase the low-voltage plateau capacity and to maintain high ICE, combination of high-temp. carbonization and low-level heteroatom doping was studied.  The P-doped hard C synthesized at 1300° with doping level of 1.1 at.% exhibits enhanced reversible capacity of 328 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1, and high ICE of 72% in SIBs.  After the P-doping, the low-voltage plateau capacity increases, while the high-voltage sloping capacity does not change significantly.  This is attributed to the enlargement of the interlayer spacing between the graphitic layers, which enhances Na+-ion intercalation.  The P-doped hard C delivers a high reversible capacity of 302 mAh g-1 in K-ion batteries (KIBs); this value is 23% larger than that of undoped hard C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrnrH8oWEbq07Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lixsmPE9TaIlQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXit1Kju73F&amp;md5=6a4279dc1f96d2b10941e0aeabe85b07</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c06543"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alhebshi, N.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fly Ash Carbon Anodes for Alkali Metal-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Jian; Zhang, Wenli; Huang, Gang; Alhebshi, Nuha A.; Salah, Numan; Hedhili, Mohamed Nejib; Alshareef, Husam N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite has become a crit. material because of its essential role in the lithium-ion battery (LIB) industry.  However, the synthesis of graphite requires an energy-intensive thermal treatment.  Also, when used in sodium-ion and potassium-ion batteries (SIBs and PIBs), the graphite anode shows poor capacities and cycling stability, which hinders the development of next-generation battery technologies.  Finding suitable anode materials for com. alkali metal-ion batteries is not only urgent for the energy storage industry, but is also important for economic and sustainable development.  In this work, we use fly ash carbon (FAC), a residue of crude oil combustion, as an anode material for alkali metal-ion batteries.  The FAC anodes show relatively high capacities and excellent cycling stability.  The charge storage mechanism of FAC anode is shown to be intercalation coupled with redox reactions of oxygen functional groups.  This work shows that FAC is a promising scalable anode material for alkali metal-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq5vLyQ8Ux0d7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lixsmPE9TaIlQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhtFOht7%252FP&amp;md5=88aa823e8851fe4f6372771489efe5d4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202013951"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kamiyama, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Igarashi, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Youn, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tateyama, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ando, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gotoh, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MgO-Template Synthesis of Extremely High Capacity Hard Carbon for Na-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Angew.     </div><div class="casAbstract">Extremely high capacity hard carbon for Na-ion battery, delivering 478 mAh g(-1) , is successfully synthesized by heating a freeze-dried mixture of magnesium gluconate and glucose by a MgO-template technique.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen and sulfur co-doped mesoporous carbon derived from ionic liquid as high-performance anode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Duan, Mingtao; Zhu, Fuliang; Zhao, Guixiang; Hu, Jian; Zhang, Hongshuai; Ren, Guofeng; Meng, Yanshuang; Fan, Zhaoyang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Microporous and Mesoporous Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">306</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">110433</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MIMMFJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1387-1811</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) are widely considered as one of the most potential alternatives to traditional lithium ion batteries (LIBs) thanks to abundance of sodium on earth.  Although these batteries have very similar electrochem., the graphite-based LIB anode cannot be directly applied for SIBs due to the much larger ionic radius of Na+.  Herein, we report nitrogen and sulfur co-doped mesoporous carbon (NSPC) as high-performance anode material for SIBs, which is synthesized via a salt template strategy with an ionic liq. as the carbon and doping source.  After carbonization, the mesoporous NSPC contains a high nitrogen content of 10.45 wt% and 1.52 wt% of sulfur with an enlarged graphite interlayer spacing to facilitate Na+ intercalation.  When used as an anode in SIBs, the NSPC shows a good electrochem. performance with a specific capacity of 243 mAh g-1 after 240 charge-discharge cycles at 0.14 A g-1.  The reversible capacity remains at 102 mAh g-1 after 5,000 cycles at 1.40 A g-1.  The high-performance of the NSPC for Na+ storage is attributed to the double doped heteroatoms and mesoporous structure, which synergistically enhance the storage capacity and rate capability, and maintain the electrode stability during cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGouAOlOWezz77Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhxAMslZ_rt2A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtlOjt7vE&amp;md5=c141ffc533777d14ddb797af14f220bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1038/nmat3601"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Augustyn, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Come, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lowe, M.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-rate electrochemical energy storage through Li+ intercalation pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Augustyn, Veronica; Come, Jeremy; Lowe, Michael A.; Kim, Jong Woung; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Abruna, Hector D.; Simon, Patrice; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">518-522</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pseudocapacitance is commonly assocd. with surface or near-surface reversible redox reactions, as obsd. with RuO2·xH2O in an acidic electrolyte.  However, we recently demonstrated that a pseudocapacitive mechanism occurs when lithium ions are inserted into mesoporous and nanocrystal films of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5; refs , ).  Here, we quantify the kinetics of charge storage in T-Nb2O5: currents that vary inversely with time, charge-storage capacity that is mostly independent of rate, and redox peaks that exhibit small voltage offsets even at high rates.  We also define the structural characteristics necessary for this process, termed intercalation pseudocapacitance, which are a cryst. network that offers two-dimensional transport pathways and little structural change on intercalation.  The principal benefit realized from intercalation pseudocapacitance is that high levels of charge storage are achieved within short periods of time because there are no limitations from solid-state diffusion.  Thick electrodes (up to 40 μm thick) prepd. with T-Nb2O5 offer the promise of exploiting intercalation pseudocapacitance to obtain high-rate charge-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPatnkXnvsNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhxAMslZ_rt2A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXlsl2jtL8%253D&amp;md5=ef16739fcf485430955b0414ac12f1ac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1126/science.1249625"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Simon, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gogotsi, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dunn, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Where Do Batteries End and Supercapacitors Begin?</span>. <i>Science</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>343</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">6176</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1210</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1211</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitive oxide materials for high-rate electrochemical energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Augustyn, Veronica; Simon, Patrice; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. energy storage technol. is based on devices capable of exhibiting high energy d. (batteries) or high power d. (electrochem. capacitors).  There is a growing need, for current and near-future applications, where both high energy and high power densities are required in the same material.  Pseudocapacitance, a faradaic process involving surface or near surface redox reactions, offers a means of achieving high energy d. at high charge-discharge rates.  Here, we focus on the pseudocapacitive properties of transition metal oxides.  First, we introduce pseudocapacitance and describe its electrochem. features.  Then, we review the most relevant pseudocapacitive materials in aq. and non-aq. electrolytes.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Facile fabrication of anode materials with low cost, good rate capability and high capacity is a crit. factor towards developing sodium-ion battery for practical applications.  Herein, a N, O co-doped porous carbon with uniform ultramicropores (NOPC-UM), is synthesized by an in-situ ultramicro templating strategy, and demonstrated as a high-performance sodium-ion storage material.  Key to this strategy is employment of an inherent KCl as ultramicro template, which leads to formation of uniform size of ultramicropores and heteroatoms (i.e., N and O) doping after high-temp. pyrolysis.  The as-constructed NOPC-UM delivers a large capacity of 305 mAh g-1, accompanying with a 93% specific capacity below 1.00 V, and superior cycling stability about 100% after 4000 cycles.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Advanced lignin-derived hard carbon for Na-ion batteries and a comparison with Li and K ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lin, Xiuyi; Liu, Yizhe; Tan, Hong; Zhang, Biao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon is the most attractive anode in Na-ion batteries.  The performance of hard carbon relies primarily on the precursors and the synthesis approaches.  Lignin, as the second-abundant biopolymer in nature, with the low cost and high carbon yield makes it an ideal precursor for the prepn. of hard carbon.  However, lignin-derived hard carbon from direct carbonization shows poor electrochem. performance.  A low-temp. pre-oxidn. is applied in this study to introduce carbonyl groups for enhancing the crosslink of lignin.  Consequently, the growth and orientation of graphitic layers during carbonization are inhibited, which in turn increases the layer distance for facilitating the Na ion insertion and leads to exceptional rate capability and superb cyclic life.  To gain insights into the charge storage mechanism, a comparison with Li- and K-ion storage in hard carbon is conducted through in-situ Raman tests.  There are similarities of alkali-metal ion storage at high voltages but remarkable disparities at low voltages, thus emphasizing the importance of microstructure design of hard carbon depending on the application in various metal-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVYwRpJvZI4LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljVIlvmVDDebQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitVKnsrjJ&amp;md5=acb321e113a28f78bfc3e17fd46310a4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1021/acs.macromol.5b02602"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Canning, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Recent progress in surface-initiated polymn. enables the deliberate polymer modification of nanoscopic surfaces with high levels of precision.  This has given rise to the development of brush particle-based materials (sometimes referred to as 'hairy nanoparticles') that are formed by tethering of polymer chains to the surface of nanoparticle-like objects.  Brush particles have attracted interest as model systems to understand the effect of surface modification on the structure and interactions in polymer modified colloidal systems (which play a role across fields as diverse as functional coatings, cosmetics, foods or pharmaceuticals) but also as building blocks for the assembly of 'one-component hybrid materials' that exhibit unprecedented property combinations, not realizable in classical composite materials.  This review presents a summary and anal. of the developments in 'particle brush materials'.  The evolution of synthetic methodologies from the original pioneering work to emerging trends and opportunities in the field of brush synthesis is presented first.  Subsequently, the effect of brush architecture on the structure, interaction and assembly of brush particles both with and without a matrix is discussed.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amorphous Carbon Chips Li-Ion Battery Anodes Produced through Polyethylene Waste Upcycling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Villagomez-Salas, Saul; Manikandan, Palanisamy; Acuna Guzman, Salvador Francisco; Pol, Vilas G.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Omega</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">17520-17527</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACSODF</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Remediation process produces high-value functional material from low-cost or valueless waste feedstock.  Current research demonstrates an innovative solvothermal approach to effectively react sulfuric acid on polyethylene (PE) chains, modifying the PE at a moderate temp.  In this process, the polymer undergoes a crosslinking step above 120 °C, whereas above 500 °C, it transforms into turbostratic carbon structures.  Scanning electron micrographs confirmed the free-standing carbon sheet architecture.  Raman spectroscopy and X-ray diffraction verified the amorphous/disordered sp2/sp3 hybrid carbon structure in the produced carbons.  A high Brunauer-Emmett-Teller surface area of 752.3 and 673.5 m2/g for low-d. PE-derived carbon (LDPE-C) and high-d. PE-derived carbon (HDPE-C), resp., was recorded.  Thermogravimetric anal. anal. established a total mass retention of 50 and 46% for LDPE and HDPE, resp., from sulfonated materials.  Li-ion battery composite anode comprising LDPE-C and HDPE-C, with a binder and a carbon additive (vs lithium), produced 230 and 350 mA h/g specific capacities for LDPE-C and HDPE-C, resp., when cycled at room temp. at C/5 rate.  Elevated temp. (50 °C) battery cycling produced 290 and 440 mA h/g specific capacities for LDPE-C and HDPE-C, resp., at C/5 rate.  On the basis of the literature survey, this is the first report, which demonstrates that a solvothermal sulfonation process followed by thermal treatment successfully converts waste LDPE and HDPE plastic bags to functional energy-storing carbons.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGok1PpjVvWbkbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhTruOTpeqk4w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXisFWqtbbF&amp;md5=be931d5a5edb42766388c6c7ee6b43ef</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1021/acssuschemeng.8b03066"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yeo, J.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Chemically Presodiated Hard Carbon Anodes with Enhanced Initial Coulombic Efficiencies for High-Energy Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Mengchuang; Zhang, Junyao; Guo, Shuhan; Wang, Bo; Shen, Yifei; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Qian, Jiangfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">17620-17627</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon (HC) is an attractive anode material for low-cost and high-energy d. sodium-ion batteries (SIBs); however, its low initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) limits its practical battery application.  To overcome this problem, we reported a facile strategy to compensate the irreversible capacity loss of HC anodes simply by a chem. presodiation reaction of the HC electrode with a sodiation reagent (sodium biphenyl, Na-Bp).  Benefiting from the strong sodiation ability of Na-Bp, HC anodes can be presodiated rapidly in a very short time and the presodiated HC (NaxHC) is found to have a desirable ICE of 100%.  When coupled with the Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode to build a SIB full cell, the NaxHC||Na3V2(PO4)3 cell exhibits a high ICE of ~ 95.0% and an elevated energy d. of 218 W h kg-1, which are far superior to those of the control cell using a pristine HC anode (50% ICE and 120 W h kg-1, resp.), suggesting great advantages brought about by the chem. presodiation process.  More importantly, this presodiation reaction is very mild and highly efficient and can be widely extended to a variety of Na-storage materials, offering a new route to develop high-performance Na-storage materials for practical battery applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoassfXRMz5d7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liq7PHemQqU2g"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Extended flat voltage profile of hard carbon synthesized using a two-step carbonization approach as an anode in sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Alvin, Stevanus; Yoon, Dohyeon; Chandra, Christian; Susanti, Ratna F.; Chang, Wonyoung; Ryu, Changkook; Kim, Jaehoon</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">430</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon is a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries (NIBs).  In this study, a two-step carbonization approach is developed to enhance the electrochem. performance of lignocellulose biomass-derived hard carbon.  The first step comprises slow low-temp. pyrolysis of fir wood that produces an amorphous carbon in which hexagonal planes are embedded in the amorphous carbon region to some extent.  The second step comprises high-temp. carbonization at 1300 °C, which yields a hard carbon with a high degree of graphitization, an increased layer-plane length, and a low micropore vol.  Two-step carbonized hard carbon delivers a large reversible capacity of 276 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 after 100 cycles and high rate capacities of 108 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 and 76.3 mAh g-1 at 2.5 A g-1.  The low-voltage plateau capacity below 0.1 V is 194 mAh g-1.  The results of these expts. indicate that the exceptional electrochem. performance of two-step carbonized hard carbon arises from the effective suppression of micropore formation and a good balance between the degree of graphitization and no. of defect sites.  High-voltage adsorption of Na+ ions in micropores inhibits Na+-ion diffusion into the graphitic region of micropore-enriched hard carbon.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6YjLSAQaWM7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liq7PHemQqU2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXpslegt7w%253D&amp;md5=e99c098987982f909806c1b21885d620</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201300071"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unveiling Intrinsic Potassium Storage Behaviors of Hierarchical Nano Bi@N-Doped Carbon Nanocages Framework via In Situ Characterizations</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Zehang; Liu, Yang; Ye, Weibin; Zhang, Jinyang; Wang, Yuyan; Lin, Yue; Hou, Linrui; Wang, Ming-Sheng; Yuan, Changzhou</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metallic bismuth has drawn attention as a promising alloying anode for advanced potassium ion batteries (PIBs).  However, serious vol. expansion/electrode pulverization and sluggish kinetics always lead to its inferior cycling and rate properties for practical applications.  Therefore, advanced Bi-based anodes via structural/compositional optimization and sur-/interface design are needed.  Herein, we develop a bottom-up avenue to fabricate nanoscale Bi encapsulated in a 3D N-doped carbon nanocages (Bi@N-CNCs) framework with a void space by using a novel Bi-based metal-org. framework as the precursor.  With elaborate regulation in annealing temps., the optimized Bi@N-CNCs electrode exhibits large reversible capacities and long-duration cyclic stability at high rates when evaluated as competitive anodes for PIBs.  Insights into the intrinsic K+-storage processes of the Bi@N-CNCs anode are put forward from comprehensive in situ characterizations.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGotcuoF939HorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liOPxTMzh1SDw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXktVOksbg%253D&amp;md5=4db97533e4d20441c8bc786855c0f8a3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201803260"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ke, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Defect-Rich Soft Carbon Porous Nanosheets for Fast and High-Capacity Sodium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Universal FeCl3-Activating Strategy for Green and Scalable Fabrication of Sustainable Biomass-Derived Hierarchical Porous Nitrogen-Doped Carbons for Electrochemical Supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Linrui; Chen, Zhiyi; Zhao, Zhiwei; Sun, Xuan; Zhang, Jinyang; Yuan, Changzhou</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">548-557</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cost-efficiency use of value-added, biomass-based carbon materials is essential for versatile electrochem. energy-related applications.  Herein, the authors smartly devised a universal and ecofriendly FeCl3-activating methodol. for scalable, high-yield fabrication of biomass-derived hierarchical porous N-doped carbons for supercapacitors.  The underlying FeCl3-involved activating mechanism was reasonably put forward.  The mushroom-derived porous N-doped carbon, as a typical FeCl3-activating example, was endowed with a large surface area of ∼1143.6 m2/g, high-fraction (∼66.3%) mesopores, high-content (∼3.1 at.%) N doping, and good wettability and exhibited even better electrochem. behaviors when compared to those activated by KOH and/or without activation, thanks to its innately structural/componental/surfacial superiorities.  The resultant carbon electrode with a high loading of 5 mg/cm2 displayed competitive gravimetric/volumetric capacitances of ∼307.4 F/g (∼212.1 F/cm3) at 1 A/g in 1 M H2SO4, much better than those in KOH, mainly owing to extra pseudocapacitance.  Also, the assembled sym. devices yielded high energy densities of ∼6.6 (1 M H2SO4) and ∼62.6 Wh/kg (1 M (TEA)BF4/PC) at a high rate of 1.5 kW/kg, and ultralong cycling performance.  More significantly, the FeCl3-involved synthetic protocol is highly promising and general for other biomass-derived porous carbon materials toward advanced supercapacitors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpWsn6pz-TtCrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liOPxTMzh1SDw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXisVOitrbI&amp;md5=20325937a94f5ff4771c51265f4de843</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201706294"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, S.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The mechanisms of lithium and sodium insertion in carbon materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Stevens, D. A.; Dahn, J. R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2001</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">148</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">A803-A811</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JESOAN</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors compare the interactions of lithium and sodium with a range of carbon materials in electrochem. cells.  Through wide angle in situ x-ray scattering studies, both lithium and sodium can be inserted into the interlayer space in disordered carbon materials.  This insertion process is accompanied by an increase in the interlayer spacing in these materials.  Small-angle in situ scattering studies are presented to clearly show the insertion of lithium and sodium into nanopores within disordered hard carbons.  Also very little, if any, sodium can be inserted into graphitic materials in contrast to the large capacity seen for lithium insertion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqOuo4QAURxurVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9BzfHFCoKtw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD3MXlvFKntr0%253D&amp;md5=15fc03ac3de24271573ed94315375242</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1039/D0EE03916K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hard carbon for sodium storage: mechanism and optimization strategies toward commercialization</span>. <i>Energy Environ. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">4</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2244</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2262</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/D0EE03916K</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D14%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D2244-2262%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26issue%3D4%26author%3DD.%2BChen%26author%3DW.%2BZhang%26author%3DK.%2BLuo%26author%3DY.%2BSong%26author%3DY.%2BZhong%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DG.%2BWang%26author%3DB.%2BZhong%26author%3DZ.%2BWu%26author%3DX.%2BGuo%26title%3DHard%2Bcarbon%2Bfor%2Bsodium%2Bstorage%253A%2Bmechanism%2Band%2Boptimization%2Bstrategies%2Btoward%2Bcommercialization%26doi%3D10.1039%252FD0EE03916K&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.2c00912&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FD0EE03916K&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hard carbon for sodium storage: mechanism and optimization strategies toward commercialization</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Dequan; Zhang, Wen; Luo, Kangying; Song, Yang; Zhong, Yanjun; Liu, Yuxia; Wang, Gongke; Zhong, Benhe; Wu, Zhenguo; Guo, Xiaodong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2244-2262</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have shown promising prospects for complementarity to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) in the field of grid-scale energy storage.  After a decade of continuous fundamental research on SIBs, it's becoming increasingly urgent to advance the commercialization.  For SIB anode materials, hard carbon is the most mature and currently the only material likely to be commercialized, but it is still far away from large-scale industrialization.  Herein, we carry out a comprehensive overview of the current state of the art in terms of three main aspects.  Firstly, a fundamental understanding of the microstructure and sodium storage mechanism of hard carbon is introduced, which can be categorized into three different processes: capacitive adsorption, nanopore filling, and intercalation in carbon interlayers.  Then, based on an in-depth understanding of the sodium storage mechanism, optimization methods in terms of increasing the specific capacity, rate performance, initial coulombic efficiency (ICE), and long-cycling stability are comprehensively summarized and analyzed.  Finally, potential methods and assocd. benefits for the design of carbon structures and the solid electrolyte interface (SEI) are discussed, hoping to provide useful guidelines for future research and commercialization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo4e0jCHDDXgrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9BzfHFCoKtw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXntlSjsb8%253D&amp;md5=d979cb5c94cd743b47028b42d41754fa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1039/D0EE01363C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Au, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alptekin, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jensen, A.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A revised mechanistic model for sodium insertion in hard carbons</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Au, Heather; Alptekin, Hande; Jensen, Anders C. S.; Olsson, Emilia; O'Keefe, Christopher A.; Smith, Thomas; Crespo-Ribadeneyra, Maria; Headen, Thomas F.; Grey, Clare P.; Cai, Qiong; Drew, Alan J.; Titirici, Maria-Magdalena</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbons have shown considerable promise as anodes for emerging sodium-ion battery technologies.  Current understanding of sodium-storage behavior in hard carbons attributes capacity to filling of graphitic interlayers and pores, and adsorption at defects, although there is still considerable debate regarding the voltages at which these mechanisms occur.  Here, ex situ23Na solid-state NMR and total scattering studies on a systematically tuned series of hard carbons revealed the formation of increasingly metallic sodium clusters in direct correlation to the growing pore size, occurring only in samples which exhibited a low voltage plateau.  Combining exptl. results with DFT calcns., we propose a revised mechanistic model in which sodium ions store first simultaneously and continuously at defects, within interlayers and on pore surfaces.  Once these higher energy binding sites are filled, pore filling occurs during the plateau region, where the densely confined sodium takes on a greater degree of metallicity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoSrEjXCn1VBrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9BzfHFCoKtw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical storage mechanism of sodium in carbon materials: A study from soft carbon to hard carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Dejian; Zhou, Xiuqing; Hu, Huanying; Li, Zhenghui; Chen, Jun; Miao, Lei; Ye, Xiaoji; Zhang, Haiyan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon materials are considered to be one of the most promising anodes for sodium ion batteries.  However, the sodium storage mechanism of carbon anodes is still in dispute.  In the current work, we prepd. a series of carbon materials ranging from soft carbon to hard carbon, with well tailorable microcrystal structure and closed pores.  By employing these carbons as anodes for sodium-ion batteries, it is interesting to find that the sodium storage in carbon materials follows an "intercalation/defect adsorption-closed pore filling" mechanism.  That is, intercalation reaction/defect adsorption contributes to sloping region in the charge/discharge curves, while the plateau region is ascribed to closed pore filling.  Furthermore, the systematical electrochem. study of soft carbon and hard carbon is implemented.  The results show that, in comparison with soft carbon, hard carbon has large sodium storage capacity owing to the incorporation of plateau region; however, the plateau region presents slow reaction kinetics, leading to relatively inferior rate performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8co9IRzfGdLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9BzfHFCoKtw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhsVOksrvI&amp;md5=1f7ec67da0cde9f5638dedca20b685c6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702434"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">3D Amorphous Carbon with Controlled Porous and Disordered Structures as a High-Rate Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Expanded biomass-derived hard carbon with ultra-stable performance in sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Ziyi; Liang, Feng; Zhou, Zhongren; Zeng, Xiaoyuan; Wang, Ding; Dong, Peng; Zhao, Jinbao; Sun, Shigang; Zhang, Yingjie; Li, Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

                        cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen, Sulfur, and Phosphorus Codoped Hollow Carbon Microtubes Derived from Silver Willow Blossoms as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Dan; Li, Shaojun; Cheng, Dejian; Miao, Lei; Zhong, Weihao; Yang, Xiaoqing; Li, Zhenghui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Fuels</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon materials have been considered as one of the most promising candidates as the anode in sodium-ion batteries.  However, scale application of state-of-the-art hard carbon anodes is still hampered on account of their complicated, toxic, and time-consuming prepn. techniques.  In the present paper, silver willow blossoms composed of natural micrometer-scale fibers are employed to construct N, S, and P codoped hollow carbon microtubes (HCMTs) by direct high-temp. carbonization.  The HCMT has a nanoscale wall with several micrometer-sized hollow cavities, which is facilitated to optimize the sodium-ion transfer.  In addn., the temp.-dependent, tailorable interlayer spacing coupled with doped heteroatoms is able to provide sufficient energy storage sites.  By combining these unique structural advantages, the HCMT exhibits impressive sodium storage performance.  The HCMT sample pyrolyzed under 1300°C is able to deliver a highly reversible capacity of 302 mAh g-1, and after repeated charge/discharge for 100 times, the capacity retains 301 mAh g-1, indicating no visible degrdn.                         cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis of N,O-codoped hard carbon on the kilogram scale for fast capacitive sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Man; Xi, Baojuan; Feng, Zhenyu; Liu, Jing; Feng, Jinkui; Qian, Yitai; Xiong, Shenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">34</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">16465-16474</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon has been identified as a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, a facile self-templating strategy has been developed for the kilogram-scale prepn. of N,O-codoped hierarchical porous hard carbon cuttlefish-like nanowire bundles (denoted as NOHPHC cuttlefishes).  The unique nanoarchitecture leads to ultrafast pseudocapacitive sodium storage, excellent reversibility, and negligible degrdn. of the host material.  NOHPHC delivers a high reversible capacity of 184 mA h g-1 at 0.5 A g-1, which is maintained at 114 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1 for over 30 000 cycles, as well as exceptional rate capability of up to 20 A g-1 with a capacity of approx. 100 mA h g-1.  Importantly, samples prepd. before and after kilogram scaling are comparable in performance.  Coupled with a Na3V2(PO4)3/C cathode, a full cell successfully obtains a high energy d. of 52.6 W h kg-1 at 50 W kg-1 and 34 W h kg-1 at 1.4 kW kg-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqmnagG_GK_SbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj3ueY-VniAtQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhsVegurbI&amp;md5=5ec49ce7f3049bb590254e3fbc5a028f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref57'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit57" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201300071"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.-G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Disordered Carbon as a Superior Anode Material for Room-Temperature Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ChemElectroChem.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">1</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">83</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">86</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Long cycle life and high rate capability of three dimensional CoSe2 grain-attached carbon nanofibers for flexible sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Hong; Qu, Hong-Qing; Liu, Zhitian; Jiang, Ren-Zhi; Li, Chong; Zhu, Ming-Qiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">58</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The flexible binderless films composed of cobalt selenide grains attached on carbon nanofibers (denoted as CoSe2/CNFs) are prepd. by electrospinning to enhance the electronic cond., Na-ions diffusion and alleviate vol. variation during charge/discharge process for high performance sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  The binderless and flexible CoSe2/CNFs electrode can obtain a high reversible capacity of 430 mAh g-1 after 400 cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1, an exceptional rate capability of 224 mAh g-1 at 15 A g-1, even a capacity of 370 mAh g-1 at 2 A g-1 after 1000 cycles.  The superior electrochem. performance can be ascribed to the synergistic effects of the homogeneous distribution of CoSe2 grains attached to the carbon nanofibers and the high electronic cond. framework of 3D interconnecting carbon nanofibers, which can alleviate the vol. variation during charge-discharge process and sustain the high elec. cond. and fast Na-ions diffusion throughout the electrode.                         cas_cit64R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">64</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-rich hierarchically porous carbon as a high-rate anode material with ultra-stable cyclability and high capacity for capacitive sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Xudong; Sun, Xiaohong; Yoo, Seung Joon; Evanko, Brian; Fan, Fengru; Cai, Shu; Zheng, Chunming; Hu, Wenbin; Stucky, Galen D.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon-based anode materials hold a promising future for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to their natural abundance and low cost of development.  In spite of carbon's important role in the commercialization of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), further exploration is necessary in order to find high-performance, high-rate carbon anode materials for SIBs.  A honeycomb-like, nitrogen-rich (17.72 at%), hierarchically porous, and highly disordered carbonaceous material (N-HC) with an expanded interlayer distance (0.44 nm in av.) is synthesized by spray drying and subsequent pyrolysis under flowing NH3.  The hierarchically porous structure and rich nitrogen doping result in a large sp. surface area (722 m2 g-1), more defects and active sites, and greater functional interface accessibility for the active porous carbonaceous material and electrolyte.  When N-HC is used as the anode material for SIBs, the batteries display favorable discharge capacities (255.9 mA h g-1 in the 3000th cycle at 500 mA g-1) and good capacitive-energy-storage behavior (67% at a scan rate of 0.5 mV s-1) with excellent high-rate performance and ultra-stable cyclability over 10,000 cycles at 5000 mA g-1.  Our results show that the combination of the hierarchically porous structure and nitrogen doping leads to improved energy storage by increasing the capacitive energy storage, which enhances the high-rate performance of N-HC.  To further enhance the performance of the material, an elec. pretreatment is employed to increase the initial Coulombic efficiency of N-HC to 79.5%, a record high for an SIB cell.  A full cell with an N-HC anode and a Na3V2(PO4)3/C cathode shows a high capacity with a favorable cyclability (238.7 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1 and a capacity retention of 95.3% compared to the second cycle).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo3JNYj3itp9rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhpgaYVGGzLlg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit65R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">65</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrahigh Phosphorus Doping of Carbon for High-Rate Sodium Ion Batteries Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Jie; Li, Haomiao; Wang, Kangli; Jin, Qianzheng; Lai, Chenglong; Wang, Ruxing; Cao, Shengling; Han, Jing; Zhang, Zhuchan; Su, Jinzhao; Jiang, Kai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phosphorus doped carbons are of particular interest as anode materials because of their large interlayer spacing and strong adsorption of Na+ ions.  However, it remains challenging to achieve high phosphorus doping due to the limited choices of phosphorus sources and the difficulty in constructing oxygen-free synthesis system.  Herein, a new synthesis strategy is proposed to prep. ultrahigh phosphorus-doped carbon (UPC) anodes for high performance sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  By using two commonly available, miscible, evaporable liqs. in PCl3 and C6H12, as phosphorus and carbon sources, an oxygen-free reaction system is successfully established by N2 bubbling to simultaneously realize carbonization and in situ P doping.  The P content can reach 30 wt%, much higher than most reported P-doping carbon-based materials.  Furthermore, the doped P is dominated by substitutional P-(C3) protrusions in the carbon lattice, which can significantly enlarge the interlayer spacing and enhance the adsorption energy of Na+.  When serving as the SIBs anode, the UPC delivers an ultrahigh reversible capacity of 510.4 mAh g-1 with a rational operating voltage of 0.54 V, and the best rate capability of 397.1 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1.  This new strategy will effectively promote the practical application of hard carbon.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp38e3qO8gFxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhpgaYVGGzLlg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit66R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">66</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sulphur-doped carbon nanosheets derived from biomass as high-performance anode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Gongyuan; Yu, Dengfeng; Zhang, Hong; Sun, Feifei; Li, Jiwei; Zhu, Lin; Sun, Lei; Yu, Miao; Besenbacher, Flemming; Sun, Ye</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">67</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted enormous attention as a promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries in recent years due to the richness and low cost of sodium (Na) resource.  The SIBs performance is essentially detd. by the electrode materials applied.  Due to the difficulty of intercalating the large Na ions, developing competent anode materials (AMs) has become particularly fascinating and crit. for SIBs.  Herein, three-dimensional (3D) scaffolding framework of carbon nanosheets heavily-doped with sulfur (S-CNS) has been fabricated from plant biomass using a facile thermal method.  The S-CNS affords an ultrahigh reversible capacity of 605 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1, high rate performance 133 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1, and long-term cycling stability at 5 A g-1 (∼94% retention upon 2000 cycles).  These values are among the best results based on AMs of doped carbon derived from biomass ever reported.  Moreover, we demonstrate that such S-doped carbon materials with competent electrochem. properties can be easily produced from diverse plant wastes using this method.  This work thus introduces a universal strategy and a fertile ground to produce high-performance AMs by using the mixt. of biomass and S powder, which may hold considerable potential for scalable prodn. of com. SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGra5olrU5vSSrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhpgaYVGGzLlg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitFKrtr3M&amp;md5=d2dfddcc08b583b1c92979075a043098</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref67"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref67'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">67</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit67" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2018.12.112"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alvin, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chandra, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cahyadi, H. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Revealing sodium ion storage mechanism in hard carbon</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>145</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">67</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">81</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.carbon.2018.12.112</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D145%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D67-81%26journal%3DCarbon%26author%3DS.%2BAlvin%26author%3DD.%2BYoon%26author%3DC.%2BChandra%26author%3DH.%2BS.%2BCahyadi%26author%3DJ.-H.%2BPark%26author%3DW.%2BChang%26author%3DK.%2BY.%2BChung%26author%3DJ.%2BKim%26title%3DRevealing%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bstorage%2Bmechanism%2Bin%2Bhard%2Bcarbon%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.carbon.2018.12.112&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.2c00912&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.carbon.2018.12.112&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit67R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">67</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Revealing sodium ion storage mechanism in hard carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Alvin, Stevanus; Yoon, Dohyeon; Chandra, Christian; Cahyadi, Handi Setiadi; Park, Jae-Ho; Chang, Wonyoung; Chung, Kyung Yoon; Kim, Jaehoon</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">145</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">67-81</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although many studies have demonstrated the excellent potential of hard carbon as an anode in sodium ion batteries, the contribution of its active sites to the capacities of the sloping and plateau voltage regions is not yet clear.  Herein, systematical investigation of the relationship between the active sites and sodium ion (Na+) storage in the sloping and plateau voltage regions was presented.  In light of the physicochem. properties of the lignin-derived hard carbon (graphitization degree, interlayer spacing, micropore size distribution, and sp. surface area), the results of Na+ ion diffusivity, and the change in these properties during Na+ ion insertion/extn. (as characterized by ex situ techniques), new mechanistic insights into Na+ ion storage were proposed.  At the beginning of the sodiation process, Na+ ions were adsorbed on defect/edge sites; then partial micropore filling occurred in the sloping region above 0.1 V.  In the plateau region below 0.1 V, Na+ ions were intercalated in the graphitic layers, and further adsorption in the micropores occurred near the cutoff potential.  Furthermore, sodium clustering occurred below 0.1 V owing to the high concn. of Na+ ions in the micropores.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoGLimnY898qLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhpgaYVGGzLlg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhtVarsLs%253D&amp;md5=38b3afcef22cf445274c04bcd7f2c3fe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref68"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref68'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">68</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit68" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201903125"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, B.                         cas_cit68R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">68</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-Supporting, Flexible, Additive-Free, and Scalable Hard Carbon Paper Self-Interwoven by 1D Microbelts: Superb Room/Low-Temperature Sodium Storage and Working Mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Bao-Hua; Wang, Ying-Ying; Ning, Qiu-Li; Li, Wen-Hao; Xi, Xiao-Tong; Yang, Xu; Liang, Hao-Jie; Feng, Xi; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">31</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1903125</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon is regarded as a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, it usually suffers from the issues of low initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) and poor rate performance, severely hindering its practical application.  Herein, a flexible, self-supporting, and scalable hard carbon paper (HCP) derived from scalable and renewable tissue is rationally designed and prepd. as practical additive-free anode for room/low-temp. SIBs with high ICE.  In ether electrolyte, such HCP achieves an ICE of up to 91.2% with superior high-rate capability, ultralong cycle life (e.g., 93% capacity retention over 1000 cycles at 200 mA g-1) and outstanding low-temp. performance.  Working mechanism analyses reveal that the plateau region is the rate-detg. step for HCP with a lower electrochem. reaction kinetics, which can be significantly improved in ether electrolyte.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpatvhKoRkPKrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhEMdPQxWJm9Q"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1039/D0TA06910H</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D8%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D20486-20492%26journal%3DJournal%2Bof%2BMaterials%2BChemistry%2BA%26issue%3D39%26author%3DN.%2BLi%26author%3DQ.%2BYang%26author%3DY.%2BWei%26author%3DR.%2BRao%26author%3DY.%2BWang%26author%3DM.%2BSha%26author%3DX.%2BMa%26author%3DL.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BQian%26title%3DPhosphorus-doped%2Bhard%2Bcarbon%2Bwith%2Bcontrolled%2Bactive%2Bgroups%2Band%2Bmicrostructure%2Bfor%2Bhigh-performance%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FD0TA06910H&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.2c00912&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FD0TA06910H&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit69R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">69</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phosphorus-doped hard carbon with controlled active groups and microstructure for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Na; Yang, Qianya; Wei, Yanxin; Rao, Richuan; Wang, Yanping; Sha, Maolin; Ma, Xiaohang; Wang, Lili; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">39</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20486-20492</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A series of phosphorus-doped hard carbon (PHC-Ts) was fabricated by directly annealing a phosphoric acid solidified epoxy resin over a wide temp. range to study the evolution of P-contg. groups and the microstructure with increasing temp., and to evaluate the Na-storage performance.  A correlation between them has been well established.  As the carbonization temp. increases, the P-contg. groups undergo a transition from P-O and P-C bonds to higher active P-P bonds with a non-monotonic decrease in the interlayer distance.  The high no. of active P-contg. groups and large interlayer distances provide more active sites and fast ion transmission channels, which jointly contribute to the excellent electrochem. performance.  The obtained PHC-700 electrodes have the largest interlayer distance and highest total activity with many P-C bonds, showing a high capacity of 379.3 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1, a superb rate capability of 158.1 mA h g-1 at 5.0 A g-1, and a long-term cycling stability without the loss of capacity after 6500 cycles at 5.0 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrm_AbhESABN7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhEMdPQxWJm9Q"> &gt;&gt;
